You noble sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its contents, and I have brought it to an end through its explanations and declarations. And it has come into my vision that I complete this for you with the treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is entirely lost everywhere, so that the science has perished and been destroyed, and nothing remains except for the small descriptions in books of the ancients which hands have moved. And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed up, and knowledge is removed.
Now it seems to me that I will bring it to life along with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will also come along with the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools of work with the joining of declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
And because of this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged. And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to ascend in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the joints of the members, and their forms, and conjunctions, and separations, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and veins, and the number of them, and their movements and rest, and the place of their origin.
And because of this, says Hippocrates that a name with its name is much, and with the work is little; and likewise in the art of hand.
We tell you in the introduction to this book that whoever is not aware of the things previously said, should beware that he does not fall into error and harm men; thus as I have often told many others who undertake this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut out, that is to say, an abscess of the scrofula or neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; wherefore so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead between his hands.
And I have seen another surgeon who treated a stone from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he carried off with him a part of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the sick man and the largeness of the stone, and knew well that if he was cut for it, he would die.
And I have seen another surgeon who took on the care of a duke from our land who had a broken leg, and with the break, there was also an open wound; and the ignorant surgeon sewed up the break over the wound with very loose stitches, and did not leave any space for drainage, and left it in this way until the leg became mortified and the foot came to destruction.
I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to loosen the leg; and when I had it untied, he was at peace and felt no pain.
But in all ways the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to progress through the member until the entire limb had been lost.
And I have seen another surgeon who burst an infected abscess, and then it inflamed through the malice of his treatment.
When the chancre is pure of melancholic humour, it is not necessary to touch it with iron if it is in such a place that everything that is corrupted can be completely removed.
And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that manual work is divided into two divisions: that is to say, the work in which there is danger in various dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and peril.
Why it is necessary for you to keep yourself safe so that the foolish man cannot speak badly of you.
Take your arms in custody, and undertake your illnesses lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised; and leave the fearful diseases with poor sanitation; and remove your weapons from those things that make you doubt, and have courage in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other one of glory.
Galien said in some of his warnings: "Do not take care of a bad illness, lest you be called a foolish physician."
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter is about cauterization with fire and medical cauterization, and it is the chapter organized from head to toe; and of the forms of instruments, and the cauterizing irons, and of all that is necessary in the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and venous bloodletting and wounds, and extracting arrowheads, and similar things; and it is the chapter that includes the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is organized from head to toe, and includes the forms of instruments.
Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of the help and harm of each complexion.
I say that the qualities of aid and its usefulness are the longest word and most subtle science and secret answer; and many of the wise spoke about these things and agreed with them; and I suffice for my words, for I am wary of their length.
I say that universal aid is to every temperament or body, whether it has matter, except for two temperaments: namely hot temperature with matter, and dry temperature with matter.
In hot and dry temperature with matter combined, they disagreed and said that cauterization is great aid; and the others said the contrary: that cauterization is not worth for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure hot disease by heat, nor dryness; and those who said the contrary say that cauterization does great aid for hot and dry disease that comes into the body of men. For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the heat of fire, you find the body cold.
And I agree with this word. For I have found it to be true once before through experience.
And in any case, no one should intervene except for those who have proven it through experience and who know from long usage the recipe of cauterization, and the diversity of human temperaments, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and remedies and the pace of time; we are not afraid of other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases. And all the physicians assembled and agreed on cauterization.
And know, my son, that fire used in cauterization is a secret of remedies, and of greater virtue than cauterization with burning medicines.
For fire is simple, and it does not affect any other member except the one that is cauterized, and it harms no other part if you know how to name its place.
The burning medicines come from one member to another by spreading and cause great harm to the sick person, and perhaps even kill him.
The fire, because of its purity and virtue of its substance, does not do this, unless there is an excess or superfluity.
And I have found this through experiment and the length of my service and study that I have devoted to this art, and it was on the truth of things; and because of this, I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for I do not like to take away from you the secret which is inherent in fire, and the quality of its work, how it beats back diseases of the body, as the philosopher says when he demonstrates it; so receive it in your thoughts.
And know, my son, that they agreed on the time when cauterizations should be done, and chose patients.
And I say that cauterization is advisable in all times, because the ensuing harm is brought under control by the aid of cauterization; and indeed if the cauterizations are for necessary, urgent pains which cannot wait until more serious harm comes to the member.
And never think that, dear son, what foolish doctors say; for the illness that is cured by cauterization has no relapse; and they say so themselves. But it's not true as they believe, because cauterizations are not just medicines that change the complexion, and dry out the humors that cause pain, but rather it's a medicine that moves quickly, because of its value, and because of the virtue of its work and its power.
And it's a great thing that the illness comes sometimes according to the complexion of the sick person and the place of the disease and its nature; and the superfluities are gathered in him through the consumption of meats and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered at the place where there is a lot of superfluity and moisture, such as cauterizations for dens pain and similar things, and that kind of pain does not come back. But it's true in some cases.
And many people don't understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and that's true; but they don't think that cauterization is worth it after medicine, but their intentions are false. And I say that cauterization is the last resort of medicine because this: when we administer other methods of treatment for a disease and they fail to work, then we administer cauterization, and it succeeds. Then it is clear that cauterization is the last of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish healers.
The ancients said that a cauterizer made of gold is more poisonous than one made of iron, and they did not say this out of ignorance but due to the quality of gold and its high substance; and they said that the wounds from cauterization do not become putrid, but it's not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that it is true in some people; and a gold cauterizer is worth more than an iron one, as they also said.
And besides, when you heat up an instrument made of gold, you don't know when it has heated enough because of the color of the gold, and it cools down at once; and if one heats it too much, it gets broken at the fire; and thus there is a lot of hindrance.
And because of that let's use iron cauterizers which we have made more suitable to our work.
Now I have ordered this chapter from the top down to the bottom, so that it may be easier for you to find.
The olive cauterizer.
These cauterizers are useful for moistening and cooling the head, and there are two of them that we use because of diseases called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the head to the temples, ears, and throat, and because of a multitude of dreams and pains in the teeth and throat, and similarly for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The shape of this cauterizer is that the sick person should be purged by a medicinal solution that clarifies the head, either three or four times, depending on what virtues, age, and habit of the sick person can tolerate; and then reheat the head of the sick person.
And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on the balance scale; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose, between his two eyes. Let your fingers come together so that he may bleed from the nose, then heat up the cauterizer called "olive" which has this form:
And put him on the place marked with ink, and do in descending and stretching your hand little by little and twisting it around; then lift up your hand suddenly, and reward the place if you see the bone .i. a small piece of gold; and if you don't see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards take .i. small handful of wool, and put in soft and moist cotton inside, and put on the place, and let him stay for .iij. days; afterwards put on damp cloth soaked in butter; and leave it on until the scab is removed; afterwards cure the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmacium", until he is healed.
And they said the old man, that the longer stays open the wound, the more it purges itself; and because of this he advised him.
And said one of them that you should burn the cautery so long that part of the bone is burned, and then redo what has been burned from the bone, and be healed.
And said the other that you should burn the cautery so long and put it so hard that it brings out of the bone as wide as a spindle that women put in their distaffs, so that the humors come out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; then it should be cured and sewn.
And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me entirely good in all cases, except that they are used in some people who have access to fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them alone. For the bones are weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we witness in other members; and likewise when the bone of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first sign of cauterization is more safe and gentle for me, and I will use this method until a good recovery.

of an abscess on the face (goule)

of a toothache (douvement des dens)
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and it doesn't work, then put the patient's head in your healthy one; after heat a cauterizer so that when you apply it to the tooth, it will come out like a rod. Put hot cautery inside immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after lift your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your pleasure. After fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let them spit for an hour and rinse well.
And in this way the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
of a toothache (dolor des dens)
When toothache pain comes from cold or if there is frostbite or water in the mouth, and medications do not work, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two ways: with a candle (cauterer de burre) and with fire.
Cauterization with a candle is done as follows: take some wax from a candle and shape it into the tip of an iron or metal spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a thread, and moisten it in melted wax. Put this on the painful tooth immediately and hold until it cools down; and do this often until the virtues of the cauterization reach the root of the tooth.
Take a hot iron or a piece of heated metal, such as brass, and make it thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth. Then heat the cauterizer until it takes shape afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer cools down; do this often, because the pain will be gone that same day or the next. And the patient must fill his mouth with good butter in the process of applying that cauterizer, and then spit out the residue; and this is the shape of the cauterizer:

of the cauterization for pleurisy (an inflammation of the lining surrounding the lungs)
The ancients said that one should make cauterizations with the roots of Aristolochia for pleurisy, in this manner: Take a long root of Aristolochia, as large as you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your arm; and soak it in oil, and then take it to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the ribcage and the neck, and two small cauterizations a little below descending in the part that is under the beard; and two cauterizations between the sixth rib and the lowest one, declining behind a little; and one cautery in the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulder blades, and two at the sides of the breast behind the cautery that is between the shoulder blades; and do not press your hand, but rather do it openly as in anointing.
And an ancient said that a man used to make a cautery of iron resembling a razor, heat it up and put it between the ribs, until it came out at the abscess; and the pain ceased, as we have said in the case of the liver abscess. of the scrotum which is called "thelul"

Of uncured wounds
When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will tell about in its place, this illness comes that can not be healed except by cauterizing.
When a boil comes and is inflamed and discharges putrid and corrupt matter, you should try to find the deepest part of it. Then cure the area as long as it takes for it to heal, and if the boil is scabbed over, and the matter has been discharged for a long time, then know that the boil is completely healed; and if the matter is not discharged, know that the boil is open and corrupted the bone at its core; and just as one of these things we will tell about in its place.

of pain from the joints

And if the pains descend to the knee and to the back, then administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter. For if you give them good governance and purge their humors, they will be healed with the help of God.
of the rupture of the spleen
When the hernia comes in angles, and the intestines descend to the scrotum and it's new, so you should instruct the patient that when you see them cure, do not harm him on that day; and he should use things that empty the belly, so that the intestines descend from his belly. Then have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to pull his intestines out as long as the hernia is repaired, and hold them at your sides, and make a sign below the hernia over the bone of the elbow, and in all one sign that is similar to half of a circle above the body. as long as it is white and he emits signs. And be aware that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are useless. And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their measure, and of big people also big according to their measure; then cure the place of the cautery with butter for three days until the scabbing is removed; then cure him with other ointments until he is healed, and have the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his swelling be calmed for a long time, so that the intestines do not burst when he gets up to go to bed.

but the first sign is the place of the navel and make a line along its width above the twisting, and another below it, and run your hands through the entire cautery with nails. But the first cauterizers are lighter and more careless.
of old pain in any member When pain comes in any member, from falling or being wounded, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary to cauterize with the cautery called "point" and the cauterization should be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of twisting and pain. If it heals from the first cauterization, that's good; if not, repeat another cauterization on top of it, because the common custom is that it should change in the member that is closest to it, so you must make the cauterizations until the sick person is healed.
of surgery (or surgical procedures)
The surgeons are helped by cauterization at times of great need, and even the diseases that come from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see them being cauterized, be careful if the disease is in its early stages, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not persist or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make 5 cauterizations on the head: 1 in the forehead at night, and another towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and 2 on the two horns, and 1 behind on the occipital bone. And leave your hand so that the cauterization reaches as far as the bone, and until the exudates of the thick humors come out; and cauterize on the wound according to what it is before you.
And if the surgery is spread throughout and it's evident that the patient will die, then it's necessary to cauterize with the cauterizations we've mentioned on the head, and 1 cauterization in the neck, and 2 cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauterizations on the spine of the back, and 1 large one on the navel and another next to it, and 2 on each shoulder, and 2 on the sides of the breast, and 2 on the tendons of the hips, and 1 on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands. And be careful not to burn the nerves that are behind the calcaneus. At times make a cauterization on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more cauterizations you make, the more help and benefit they bring; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cauterization if it is similar to a healthy person, because the body is already completely corrupted. And it's necessary that the cauterizations are large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find them in various types of irons.
of swelling
When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines and oils and poultices, but it is not healed, then you should make blisters on the limb according to its size and smallness; and let the blister be one inch going into the depth of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes one makes a blister at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but otherwise no doctor should interfere if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the outlets of the moving nerves in the body.
of ulcers
When the disease called "ulcer" is deep-rooted, and no medicine can do anything about it, then cauterize it with a blister one inch deep, according to the depth of the flesh, until the ulcer is removed and its color changes; then cure it with flour of poppy seeds and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and vinegar from gall and red wine, each in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it at the fire until it is healed.
the treatment of syphilis by blistering
When the chancre comes to begin, and you see it stop growing, if you cauterize with a fire that appears as one circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And wise men have said that we should also make a cauterization in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen at least once; and a more correct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the fire that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
of swelling that cannot die
When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it takes too long to die or because of the superfluity that it causes, or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, very old) and he has pus in his veins, or because of the tension; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries that are burning; after that leave him so. For it will hasten to die.
And if you see it piercing through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterization until its form is changed:
And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauterization has pierced to the bone, and let the cauterization be such that the patient feels it from outside in a way that makes the course of the purulence to be alleviated. Then cure him as long as he is perfectly healthy.
the cure with fire by iron (or, possibly) the surgical cure by iron (i.e. surgery performed with a hot iron or cautery)
Another manner of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a gangrenous member, for it gnaws the members just like fire gnaws dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can suffer cauterization with fire, then heat up small and large cauteries according to what is needed at the site of the disease; after that cauterize from all sides until you remove all the corruption, and leave nothing but what is sound. And then let it be for three days, and put salve on the cauterized place so that it broils with oil until the burns of fire are removed, and all the corruption. After that cure with ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh has not grown, it's good; and if not, then resume the cauterization on what remains from the corrupted places. And this gangrene has been cured sometimes by medicine instead of cauterization with fire; but nevertheless, cauterization with fire is a greater aid, and I have already said the cure with medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
The spurs which come to the feet
The swelling that comes to the feet is often a disease called "clou" as we intend it, and is a large, ugly thing that wounds the foot. And the treatment for this disease is in two ways: fire cautery, and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is when you heat one cautery as sharp as an awl's point, and make it out of good iron to its size, so that it can pierce the swelling from all sides, and have subtle margins; then place it all hot on the swelling, and turn your hand completely around the swelling until it comes to the temperature of the swelling; and let it be like that for three days until it begins to fall off; then make a poultice with bitter savin berries pounded with vinegar, and leave the poultice on overnight, and the swelling will come out and its roots will be pulled out. Then cure the place with ointment spreading char until it is healed.
And if they are converted by the body, and it happens often in hands and on feet, you should apply hot water cautery; and it is in this manner: take a tin or iron cylinder, or an awl point, and place it on the boil and the surrounding area, that is, the spurs and warts; and place the cylinder on so that it pierces all around, then put a little hot water in it, and keep your hand firm, and press your hand while turning it so that the edge of the cylinder comes to the root of the boil, and allows the hot water to penetrate deep to the root; and let the patient feel the burning sensation of the hot water for an hour; then leave it alone, and it will come out with all its roots. Do this again and again until you have extracted all those that are in the body, then cure them with ointments that make char.

boils that pus
Sometimes appearing on the body from the outside, or boils that pus, which come from great corrupted matter. It is necessary at first when they appear to make a cautery on each head of the boil: a subtle cautery from a hawthorn stick, whose point has been seized by fire, or from a root of aristolochia longa, or a lentil cautery. when the artery is cut Often there are great outflows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the outside, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the member, and suchlike things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
And yet when this happens to someone, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press hard until the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more comes out; then take olive cauteries, both small and large, as many as they are red, and then catch one, either great or small according to the wound and its place where the artery runs, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery so long as the bleeding is stopped.
And if it bursts out again when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery cools down, then take hastily another one of the cauteries that are on the fire.
And do not stop doing these one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the sick person. And know that when blood spurts from an artery, it cannot be well stopped directly if the artery is large, except by one of the four ways we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not tied off, or by strongly tying a thread, or by medicines applied which have power to stop bleeding; and it should be tied and strained properly.
Who would remind of the danger of stopping bleeding with tightly tied strings or by applying hot things on top, or similar things, if they did not have some effect?
And if this happens to someone and they do not have a physician or medicine present, then they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we said, and press hard until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and they must not move their finger, but moisten it with cold water frequently so that it is very cold, until the bleeding is congealed and thickened and stopped. And make inquiries in front to get what they need of cauteries and medicines.
We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases in which one must cautery with fire, or with a burning medicine, and the instruments and causes and the forms of cauterization; and I put that chapter at the head until now, and I will go into this chapter by the same way so that you may find more easily what you want.
And thus that I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterization, and therefore it is necessary to be on greater guard.
For in the work of this chapter there are many times evacuation of blood at opening the vein, and at incising above an aposteme, and at dressing wounds, and at extracting splinters, and at incising on the bone, and similar things; or there is danger and fear, and death comes to many.
And I advise you that you not take foolishness upon yourselves. For many kinds of people come to be cured. Some come who are so beset with their illness that they will soon die from the recklessness they find in their disease, and from the great severity of their malice; and of these one should have fear. And among these are those who will give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the disease is spiteful. The chapters of abscesses
Many kinds of abscesses are described in this book, which differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one occurs as much the same, and because it is moist. And the second way is when they occur in the flesh itself. For abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of fatty flesh are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in its work.
And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its completion; and those that require piercing when they are old, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that occur near joints. For when an abscess comes near a joint, and you leave it until it is putrid around it, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint will be corrupted, causing contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is next to the principal limb, and you delay piercing it until it is dead, you will harm the principal limb; or if it is next to the foundation, then pierce it when it is dead; but do not pierce an old, unhealed abscess, except for one that is near the foundation, lest it suppurate deep inside and become a fistula, and be unable to heal in a long time.
And it is necessary that you know the work of piercing an abscess that has died according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the cessation of movement and tension at the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the puncture over or as close as possible to the place where the abscess has opened up, and where it protrudes; and that the puncture be long enough to reach the core of the abscess. And if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or near joints and nerves and arteries, then in all places equally, there is no need for a poultice.
When swellings occur, follow the same member. And when an abscess is in its natural place, it's worth noting that you should leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, the body will be drained of venom and will be full of pus; and perhaps the lips and the deepest parts of it will become hardened. And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, follow them in the same way as they need for their members. Concerning circumcision
Circumcision is not the removal of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this act on our own free will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the most light for health.
I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Because I have seen the majority of masters and sages who performed circumcision were around one year old, strong, and had all their teeth; the boys cried because they had two foreskins, and perhaps someone hit them above and left the lower skin alone.
Now they cover it up, and the pain is doubled, and there is the infection which to the one year old child is not sure the point of the limb; and the infection of the angle by chance misses the iron, and the work runs away, and many times are born in such a way that they do not need cleaning and I have seen this.
Concerning the cleaning that is done to the strong ones (children) I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the foreskins cut just as well above as below.
Because when you press your hand, it cuts equally well in both directions; but the thread must be very thin around the skin; and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only going to tie a thread around the penis as much as possible, and then you do it in all ways that you can. hermaphrodites
Hermaphroditism is in two ways like men: the one way is that between the two testicles it opens out as much as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes on the outside it urinates. of the unicorn

From hemorrhoids.
Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which, without proper care, normally close up by themselves, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn into a scab. We have already discussed their similarities and signs in the division, and now I will say those which receive cure. I say that hemorrhoids and the scab, if they are deep inside the anus and cannot be felt, do not need treatment except by iron. Those which are at the entrance of the anus, where one can feel them, are the ones which can be treated. It is necessary for you to put the woman in a cold house, then tie up the scab with tweezers, and then powder over medicines constricting blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then place her feet on it for an hour, then put them in cold water. And if bleeding comes from it, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and the bark of pomegranate and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour and mix it with honey and gall, and make .i. plaster on her back. And if it heals, that is good. If not, make her have ventouses on her back and shoulders without ironing them; then take linen, and wet it in plantain juice or in agnus castus juice with old wine, and make it warm up. And when the swelling subsides, cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to .i. rough head, so it should be scraped as I said about the scab; and then cure it until it is healed.

of childbirth
It is necessary for the midwife to know the natural figure of childbirth and its signs; when you see the woman pressing down, and desiring to urinate: then the child hastens to come out in force; thus you should recognize that this birth is according to the natural figure, and the head comes out first, and the second part with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press her stomach lightly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it comes up to its head, the second part comes with it, and the body is freed of its superfluous parts by good purgation; and what does not come in this way does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes on its feet, and comes out through the joints or hands, or it comes up onto its stomach, or side, and turns around by chance to its neck, and by other bad figures; thus it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help her.
If the child comes out with its head first in natural delivery, and the woman is giving birth easily, and her pains are weak, then have her sit on a stool, or women hold it for her; and apply some oil or fenugreek to her nature, which should be cooked, and then insert the midwife between her thighs with this small spatula of this shape: It's worth noting that the text is written in Middle French and contains some archaic language and medical practices that may not be suitable for modern readers. of wounds.
We have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds; and now we will speak of the treatments for hands and medicines, according to their fulfillment.
I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the place or location where they are made, and of what they are made.
The things by which wounds are made are by cutting with a stone, and hacking with a sword or knife, or a lance or fist or spear, or similar things.
or that are made according to the parts of the body, such as wounds that cut on the neck, or on the head, or on the chest, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members.
and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory comes to its chapter.
I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, you must be careful if it was caused by cutting with a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large. and you doubt that it is a hot aposteme (infection), if you make it heal quickly with the application of head oil itself, even if there is pus coming from the wound, and the healing is on the contrary side of the injured area.
and give the patient a drink of wine and feed them large quantities of meat.
And if it does not want to heal, then make the patient's food less rich and do not let them drink wine or eat meat.
and put a compress on the wound, if hot aposteme comes, soaked cotton in rose oil or vinegar.
and if there is no hot aposteme, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and not dried by air or powder, which I will tell you about later.
and if the wound has dried, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips of the wound cannot be joined together by stitches, then join them together with a suture, just as I will say about belly wounds in the chapter on suturing.
If the wound is open to the bone and swollen, and it holds together only by a small strip of skin, then cut away the dead tissue. Then treat the wound with medicine, and replace tough meat in place of the skin. and command the patient to eat large quantities of meat, such as roasted testicles and bread, as well as poultry and similar things.
And if you find or see purulence in the skin that has not reached the bone, then cut out all the purulent part and let it bleed, then treat the wound.
and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that is cut and cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie the artery, and if you find it loose, then tie it with a thread. and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and it is that you put in this powder that closes the wound even when the fire has dried it.
And the manner of making this powder is: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; and three parts of powdered sal ammoniac, and grind it finely. and fill the wound with this powder, and apply pressure, until it dries well and joins together with all its blood.
and then bind it tightly, and let it be without being undone, if it does not become inflamed; because the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
And sometimes one makes this powder solely of sal ammoniac, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the fire has dried the wound.
And if the fire has completely dried the wound, even to the bone, then do not put this powder on it.
but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices made with barley flour cooked in water and honey, until it runs like pus. then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers.
and I will tell you about skull fractures later.
of the wound of the neck.
If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery are cut.

but put on medicated oil, such as sal ammoniac dissolved in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber juice also dissolved in sweet water. and other medicines of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.

of the wound from a lance or knife.
If it is a wound from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, then observe if there are signs of gangrene spreading to the surrounding flesh of the patient. If you see this, then know that the wound is mortal.
and if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder on it at first hour, nor bind it tightly so that the blood does not dry in depth. and the patient recovers to their heart's content, and the patient dies. but I put on attractive ointment, and bind it two times a day.
and if you don't have ointment, then put clean cotton in the wound to suck out any remaining moisture.

The ulcers
Warts are thick, swollen, and filled with foul-smelling fluid that come on many members of the body.
and they occur more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens than in others.

The treatment of warts is in two ways: one is to cut them off and let the black blood dry out; and the other way is that you bind the wart with a thread and let it dry completely.

This is the beginning of the Book of Bruises.
These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and are a restoration for bruising and purging.
Listen, dear son, the foolish multitude throws themselves from this chapter, which they never found in any ancient book or letter.
and because of this reason is the science estranged in our land, for I have never found a good one;
and I know nothing about it, except by the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much and treated in a scientific way, and through experience, and by the habit of my life.
